Implemented fixes for the real runtime failures in your logs.

**What I changed**
- Fixed the XLS writer stream-lifetime bug that caused `System.ObjectDisposedException: Cannot access a closed file` during temp save/replace by keeping the source `FileStream` alive until save completes and disposing in `finally` (Service_XLSWriter.cs, Service_XLSWriter.cs).
- Kept duplicate DB inserts idempotent but stopped counting duplicate-key rows as newly saved records, so save counts are accurate (Dao_ReceivingLoad.cs).
- Added a workflow warning when some loads were skipped because they already existed, instead of silently looking like full inserts (Service_ReceivingWorkflow.cs).

**Validation**
- Solution build passes successfully (same pre-existing warnings only, no new errors from these changes).

**Notes**
- The long “Cannot find or open the PDB file” debugger lines are normal for framework/third-party assemblies.
- The `Settings decrypt failed: Padding is invalid...` message is a separate environment/config secret issue (not from these save-path fixes).

User: In C#, the default behavior for opening an XLSX file is to lock it for exclusive access by the first user, forcing subsequent users to open it as read-only. To allow multiple users to open and edit the file simultaneously, you must implement specific strategies, as the standard file system access does not inherently support this for file-based Excel files. 
Here are the recommended approaches for enabling multi-user access via C#:
1. Use the FileShare Enumeration (for concurrent reads/writes) 
When using file streams to interact with the file (often the underlying mechanism for C# Excel libraries), you can specify a FileShare mode to allow multiple processes to interact with the file at the same time. 
FileShare.ReadWrite: This allows subsequent users to open the file for both reading and writing while it is already open.
Caveat: This approach only works if your Excel library or specific implementation properly handles the concurrent changes without data corruption. Standard Excel behavior (even with FileShare.ReadWrite) will likely still have issues with conflicting changes if not managed correctly. 
Example using FileStream (low-level file access):
csharp
using System.IO;

// Open the file with read/write permissions for current user 
// and allow other users to also open for read/write
using (FileStream fs = new FileStream(filePath, FileMode.Open, FileAccess.ReadWrite, FileShare.ReadWrite))
{
    // Pass the stream to your C# Excel library (e.g., OpenXML, NPOI)
    // to read or write data.
}
This approach is useful for libraries that work with streams, such as the Open XML SDK or NPOI. 
2. Implement a Database or Middleware Approach 
For robust, concurrent multi-user access with data integrity, the most reliable method is to avoid direct file system access for simultaneous edits. Instead, use a shared database to store the data and then generate the Excel file on demand. 
Multiple users can read from and write to the database simultaneously without file locking issues.
Your C# application can then use a library like NPOI or Open XML SDK to export the current database data into an XLSX file whenever a user requests it.
3. Leverage Excel's Built-in Co-authoring (Cloud-based) 
If you are using modern Excel versions (Office 365) and the files are hosted on OneDrive or SharePoint, co-authoring is enabled by default. This allows multiple users to edit the file in real-time. 
Your C# application would interact with the file via the relevant Microsoft Graph API or SharePoint services rather than the local file path. 
4. Open in Read-Only Mode and Use a Copy for Edits 
If users only need to read the main file but their edits are temporary or saved elsewhere, you can open the file in read-only mode in C#. 
Example using Excel Interop (not recommended for server use):
csharp
using Microsoft.Office.Interop.Excel;

var app = new Microsoft.Office.Interop.Excel.Application();
// Open as ReadOnly
var workbook = app.Workbooks.Open(filename, ReadOnly: true);
// ... do work ...
workbook.Close();
app.Quit();
Alternatively, copy the original file to a temporary, local location and open the copy for editing. The original file will remain accessible to all other users. 
In summary, the best default option in C# for truly concurrent, multi-user access with editing capabilities is to use a robust data management strategy (like a database) or leverage cloud storage with co-authoring. Direct manipulation of local XLSX files by multiple users via C# is generally not a reliable solution for simultaneous editing without potential data conflicts.

**What changed**

- Updated fallback write call to `append: false` so each fallback file is created as a fresh standalone file, avoiding lock/contention collisions between users/sessions.
- Updated log/error text to explicitly indicate “shared fallback file” behavior.

User: look at the following code and incorperate it if it is not already.  remove any unneeded code that the following will make obsolete.  using ClosedXML.Excel;
using DocumentFormat.OpenXml.Packaging;
using DocumentFormat.OpenXml.Spreadsheet;
using System.IO;

// ... other using statements from your original code

private async Task WriteToFileAsync(string filePath, List<Model_ReceivingLoad> loads, bool append = true)
{
    using (var workbook = File.Exists(filePath) ? new XLWorkbook(filePath) : new XLWorkbook())
    {
        var worksheet = workbook.Worksheets.FirstOrDefault() ?? workbook.Worksheets.Add("Receiving Data");

        // Logic to add your 'loads' data to the worksheet here...
        // Example: worksheet.Cell(1, 1).Value = "Sample Data";

        // IMPORTANT: Enable Shared Workbook (Legacy) before saving
        EnableWorkbookSharing(workbook);

        workbook.SaveAs(filePath);
    }
}

/// <summary>
/// Injects OpenXML parts required to enable the "Shared Workbook" (Legacy) feature.
/// </summary>
private void EnableWorkbookSharing(XLWorkbook workbook)
{
    // Access the underlying OpenXML WorkbookPart
    var workbookPart = workbook.WorkbookPart;

    // 1. Add WorkbookUserDataPart (Stores info on users with the file open)
    if (workbookPart.WorkbookUserDataPart == null)
    {
        var userDataPart = workbookPart.AddNewPart<WorkbookUserDataPart>();
        userDataPart.Users = new Users(); 
    }

    // 2. Add WorkbookRevisionHeaderPart (Required for change tracking in shared mode)
    if (workbookPart.WorkbookRevisionHeaderPart == null)
    {
        var revisionHeaderPart = workbookPart.AddNewPart<WorkbookRevisionHeaderPart>();
        revisionHeaderPart.Headers = new Headers { Guid = Guid.NewGuid().ToString("B") };
        
        // Add a log part for tracking revisions
        revisionHeaderPart.AddNewPart<WorkbookRevisionLogPart>();
    }
}
